Your objective is to generate a compilable CBMC harness for a provided C function:

You will be provided with the name and implementation of the target function. 
Additionally, you have access to the following tools:

1. Bash tool: This tool will allow you to run bash commands such as grep that can help search the repo for relevant information. 
2. CScope tool: The target repository has already been indexed with cscope. This tool allows you to run cscope commands to retrieve type definitions, function cross-references, and full paths to specific files.

Here are sample cscope commands to run:
# --- Symbol and function lookups ---
cscope -dL -1 <symbol>        # Find where symbol/function is defined
cscope -dL -0 <symbol>        # Find all references to symbol/function
cscope -dL -2 <func>          # Find functions called by <func>
cscope -dL -3 <func>          # Find functions calling <func>

# --- File and include lookups ---

# --- Type and text searches ---

cscope -dL -9 typedef\ <name> # Find typedef definitions
cscope -dL -4 <text>          # Find occurrences of text
cscope -dL -6 <symbol>        # Find assignments to symbol

You must follow these steps strictly:
1. Include the path to the file containing the target function at the top of the harness. The specific path to include is provided in the user prompt below. This is to ensure the harness can access static symbols and other struct definitions defined in the file.
2. Define a harness called `void harness()`.
3. Declare all function parameters inside `harness` exactly as they appear in the function signature.
4. For any input pointer argument (e.g., `uint8_t *data`, `struct my_struct *ptr`), do the following:
    - Create a pointer size variable of type size_t (e.g., `size_t data_len`, `size_t ptr_len`) to hold the allocation size.
    - If the pointer is a struct pointer, constrain the minimum size of the pointer size variable to the size of the struct using __CPROVER_assume. (e.g., __CPROVER_assume(ptr_len >= sizeof(struct mystruct))).
    - Initialize the pointer by allocating memory using the size variable `uint8_t *data = malloc(data_len); struct my_struct *ptr = malloc(ptr_len);` 
5. Finally, call the function in the harness using the declared and initialized arguments.
6. Do NOT make any additional constraints in the harness.

void harness() {

}

<function_source>
static int _receive(gnrc_pktsnip_t *pkt)
{
    TCP_DEBUG_ENTER;
    /* NOTE: In receiving direction: pkt = payload, payload->next = tcp, tcp->next = nw */
    uint16_t ctl = 0;
    uint16_t src = 0;
    uint16_t dst = 0;
    uint8_t hdr_size = 0;
    uint8_t syn = 0;
    gnrc_pktsnip_t *ip = NULL;
    gnrc_pktsnip_t *reset = NULL;
    gnrc_tcp_tcb_t *tcb = NULL;
    tcp_hdr_t *hdr;

    /* Get write access to the TCP header */
    gnrc_pktsnip_t *tcp = gnrc_pktbuf_start_write(pkt);
    if (tcp == NULL) {
        gnrc_pktbuf_release(pkt);
        TCP_DEBUG_ERROR("-EACCESS: Can't write to packet.");
        TCP_DEBUG_LEAVE;
        return -EACCES;
    }
    pkt = tcp;

#ifdef MODULE_GNRC_IPV6
    /* Get IPv6 header, discard packet if doesn't contain an ip header */
    ip = gnrc_pktsnip_search_type(pkt, GNRC_NETTYPE_IPV6);
    if (ip == NULL) {
        gnrc_pktbuf_release(pkt);
        TCP_DEBUG_ERROR("-EBADMSG: Packet contains no IPv6 header.");
        TCP_DEBUG_LEAVE;
        return -EBADMSG;
    }
#endif

    /* Get TCP header */
    tcp = gnrc_pktsnip_search_type(pkt, GNRC_NETTYPE_TCP);
    if (tcp == NULL) {
        gnrc_pktbuf_release(pkt);
        TCP_DEBUG_ERROR("-EBADMSG: Packet contains no TCP header.");
        TCP_DEBUG_LEAVE;
        return -EBADMSG;
    }

    if (tcp->size < sizeof(tcp_hdr_t)) {
        gnrc_pktbuf_release(pkt);
        TCP_DEBUG_ERROR("-EBADMSG: Packet size less than minimal header size.");
        TCP_DEBUG_LEAVE;
        return -EBADMSG;
    }

    /* Extract control bits, src and dst ports and check if SYN is set (not SYN+ACK) */
    hdr = (tcp_hdr_t *)tcp->data;
    ctl = byteorder_ntohs(hdr->off_ctl);
    src = byteorder_ntohs(hdr->src_port);
    dst = byteorder_ntohs(hdr->dst_port);
    syn = ((ctl & MSK_SYN_ACK) == MSK_SYN);

    /* Validate offset */
    if (GET_OFFSET(ctl) < TCP_HDR_OFFSET_MIN) {
        gnrc_pktbuf_release(pkt);
        TCP_DEBUG_ERROR("-ERANGE: Invalid TCP header offset.");
        TCP_DEBUG_LEAVE;
        return -ERANGE;
    }

    /* Calculate TCP header size */
    hdr_size = GET_OFFSET(ctl) * 4;

    /* Mark TCP header if it contains any payload */
    if ((pkt->type == GNRC_NETTYPE_TCP) && (pkt->size != hdr_size)) {
        tcp = gnrc_pktbuf_mark(pkt, hdr_size, GNRC_NETTYPE_TCP);
        if (tcp == NULL) {
            gnrc_pktbuf_release(pkt);
            TCP_DEBUG_ERROR("-ENOMSG: Header marking failed.");
            TCP_DEBUG_LEAVE;
            return -ENOMSG;
        }
        pkt->type = GNRC_NETTYPE_UNDEF;
        hdr = (tcp_hdr_t *)tcp->data;
    }

    /* Validate checksum */
    if (byteorder_ntohs(hdr->checksum) != _gnrc_tcp_pkt_calc_csum(tcp, ip, pkt)) {
#ifndef MODULE_FUZZING
        gnrc_pktbuf_release(pkt);
        TCP_DEBUG_ERROR("-EINVAL: Invalid checksum.");
        TCP_DEBUG_LEAVE;
        return -EINVAL;
#endif
    }

    /* Find TCB to for this packet */
    _gnrc_tcp_common_tcb_list_t *list = _gnrc_tcp_common_get_tcb_list();
    mutex_lock(&list->lock);
    tcb = list->head;
    while (tcb) {
#ifdef MODULE_GNRC_IPV6
        /* Check if current TCB is fitting for the incoming packet */
        if (ip->type == GNRC_NETTYPE_IPV6 && tcb->address_family == AF_INET6) {
            /* If SYN is set, a connection is listening on that port ... */
            ipv6_addr_t *tmp_addr = NULL;
            _gnrc_tcp_fsm_state_t state = _gnrc_tcp_fsm_get_state(tcb);
            if (syn && tcb->local_port == dst && state == FSM_STATE_LISTEN) {
                /* ... and local addr is unspec or pre configured */
                tmp_addr = &((ipv6_hdr_t *)ip->data)->dst;
                if (ipv6_addr_equal((ipv6_addr_t *) tcb->local_addr, (ipv6_addr_t *) tmp_addr) ||
                    ipv6_addr_is_unspecified((ipv6_addr_t *) tcb->local_addr)) {
                    break;
                }
            }

            /* If SYN is not set and the ports match ... */
            if (!syn && tcb->local_port == dst && tcb->peer_port == src) {
                /* .. and the IPv6 addresses match */
                tmp_addr = &((ipv6_hdr_t * )ip->data)->src;
                if (ipv6_addr_equal((ipv6_addr_t *) tcb->peer_addr, (ipv6_addr_t *) tmp_addr)) {
                    break;
                }
            }
        }
#else
        /* Suppress compiler warnings if TCP is built without network layer */
        TCP_DEBUG_ERROR("Missing network layer. Add module to makefile.");
        (void) syn;
        (void) src;
        (void) dst;
#endif
        tcb = tcb->next;
    }
    mutex_unlock(&list->lock);

    /* Call FSM with event RCVD_PKT if a fitting TCB was found */
    /* cppcheck-suppress knownConditionTrueFalse
     * (reason: tcb can be NULL at runtime)
     */
    if (tcb != NULL) {
        _gnrc_tcp_fsm(tcb, FSM_EVENT_RCVD_PKT, pkt, NULL, 0);
    }
    /* No fitting TCB has been found. Respond with reset */
    else {
        if ((ctl & MSK_RST) != MSK_RST) {
            _gnrc_tcp_pkt_build_reset_from_pkt(&reset, pkt);
            if (gnrc_netapi_send(_tcp_eventloop_pid, reset) < 1) {
                gnrc_pktbuf_release(reset);
                TCP_DEBUG_ERROR("Can't dispatch to network layer.");
            }
        }
        TCP_DEBUG_ERROR("-ENOTCONN: Unable to find matching TCB.");
        TCP_DEBUG_LEAVE;
        return -ENOTCONN;
    }
    gnrc_pktbuf_release(pkt);
    TCP_DEBUG_LEAVE;
    return 0;
}

</function_source>

For example:\n * ```\n * if (IS_ACTIVE(FEATURE_FOO)) {\n *      do_something();\n * }\n * ```\n * @param[in]   macro   Macro to evaluate\n * @returns     1 if the macro is defined to 1\n * @returns     0 if the macro is not defined, of if it is defined to something\n *              else than 1.\n *\n * @note        This should only be used when macros are defined as 1, it will\n *              not work if the macro value is, for example, (1) or 1U.\n *\n * @note        Although this may seem to work similarly to the preprocessor\'s\n *              \'defined\', it is not entirely equal. If the given macro has\n *              been defined with no value, this will expand to 0. Also note\n *              that this is intended to be used with \'boolean\' macros that act\n *              as switches, and usually will be defined as 1 or not defined.\n */\n#define IS_ACTIVE(macro) __is_active(macro)\n\n/**\n * @def         IS_USED(module)\n * @brief       Checks whether a module is being used or not. Can be used in C\n *              conditionals.\n *\n * @param[in]   module   Module to check\n * @returns     1 if the module is being used\n * @returns     0 if the module is not being used\n */\n#define IS_USED(module) IS_ACTIVE(module)\n\n/**\n * @cond INTERNAL\n */\n/* Here a prefix "__PREFIX_WHEN_" is added to the macro. So if it was a 1 we\n * have "__PREFIX_WHEN_1", and if it was not defined we have "__PREFIX_WHEN_".\n */\n#define __is_active(val)              ___is_active(__PREFIX_WHEN_##val)\n\n/* With this placeholder we turn the original value into two arguments when the\n * original value was defined as 1 (note the comma).\n */\n#define __PREFIX_WHEN_1 0,\n\n/* Here we add two extra arguments, that way the next macro can accept varargs.\n *\n * If the original macro was defined as 1, this will have three arguments\n * (__take_second_arg(0, 1, 0, 0)), otherwise it will have two\n * (__take_second_arg(__PREFIX_WHEN_ 1, 0, 0)). The third zero is there just to\n * be compliant with C99, which states that when a function-like macro ends\n * with ellipsis (...) it should be called with at least one argument for the\n * variable list.\n */\n#define ___is_active(arg1_or_junk)    __take_second_arg(arg1_or_junk 1, 0, 0)\n\n/* Finally, we just always take the second argument, which will be either 1\n * (when three arguments are passed, i.e. macro was defined as 1) or 0 (when\n * only two arguments are passed).\n */\n#define __take_second_arg(__ignored, val, ...) val\n/**\n * @endcond\n */\n\n#ifdef __cplusplus\n}\n#endif\n\n/** @} */\n', 'stderr': ''}

2026-03-30 15:46:16,635 [INFO] (makefile_generator.py:147) System Prompt:
You are a helpful AI assistant that generates Makefiles for CBMC proof harnesses.
Your objective is to analyze the target source file and the proof harness, and produce a working Makefile that compiles the harness and target file in isolation for unit-level CBMC verification.

## Makefile Structure

The Makefile has the following key fields that you can modify:
1. **H_INC**: Include paths (-I flags) needed to resolve header file dependencies.
2. **H_DEF**: Preprocessor definitions (-D flags) for configuration macros that the source file depends on.
3. **H_CBMCFLAGS**: Flags passed to CBMC during analysis. You typically do not need to modify this for build errors.
4. **LINK**: Additional source files to link into the harness.

## Your Approach

You should follow this workflow:

1. **Analyze the target file**: Study the harness code and identify which headers are included (directly and transitively). Use the provided tools (bash commands, cscope) to locate these header files in the project.
2. **Identify include paths**: For each header that may not be found by default, determine the correct `-I` path to add to `H_INC`.
3. **Identify configurations**: Examine the target source file and its headers for `#ifdef`, `#if defined(...)`, and similar preprocessor guards. Determine which configuration macros (`-D` flags) must be set under `H_DEF` to enable the relevant code paths.
4. **Update and test the Makefile**: Use the `makefile_validator` tool to write your proposed Makefile and run `make compile`. The tool returns the compilation result (exit code, stdout, stderr).
5. **Iterate**: If compilation fails, analyze the error, adjust H_INC, H_DEF, or LINK as needed, and call `makefile_validator` again. Repeat until compilation succeeds.
6. **Return your final response**: Once compilation succeeds, return your analysis and the final working Makefile.

## Available Tools

1. **run_bash_command**: Run bash commands (e.g., `grep`, `find`, `head`) to search the repository for header files, configuration macros, and other relevant information.
2. **run_cscope_command**: The target repository has been indexed with cscope. Use this to find definitions, cross-references, and file paths.
3. **makefile_validator**: Write a complete Makefile and run `make compile`. Returns the compilation result so you can iterate on errors.

### Sample cscope commands:
```
# --- Symbol and function lookups ---
cscope -dL -1 <symbol>        # Find where symbol/function is defined
cscope -dL -0 <symbol>        # Find all references to symbol/function
cscope -dL -2 <func>          # Find functions called by <func>
cscope -dL -3 <func>          # Find functions calling <func>

# --- File and include lookups ---
cscope -dL -7 <filename>      # Find full path to file
cscope -dL -8 <header>        # Find files including this header

# --- Type and text searches ---
cscope -dL -9 struct\ <name>  # Find struct definitions
cscope -dL -9 typedef\ <name> # Find typedef definitions
cscope -dL -4 <text>          # Find occurrences of text
cscope -dL -6 <symbol>        # Find assignments to symbol
```

# Defines the root of the project.
# Be aware of how many directories deep you go!
ROOT = ../../..

# Defines file(s) to link to harness, MUST be a full path!
# (We recommend $(ROOT)/os/... for defining these paths)
# Each file is space seperated, and multiple can be defined
LINK = $(ROOT)/sys/net/gnrc/network_layer/sixlowpan/frag/rb/gnrc_sixlowpan_frag_rb.c 

# Harness to utilize, omit the extension!
H_ENTRY = _rbuf_add

# Extra CBMC flags to be passed during CBMC analysis
H_CBMCFLAGS = --nondet-static --unwind 1 --unwindset gnrc_sixlowpan_frag_rb_gc.2:2 \
       --unwindset _rbuf_int_get_free.0:2 \
       --unwindset _check_fragments.1:2 --unwindset gnrc_pkt_delete.0:2


H_DEF = -DGNRC_NETTYPE_SIXLOWPAN=1 -DMODULE_GNRC_SIXLOWPAN_FRAG=1 -DMODULE_GNRC_SIXLOWPAN_FRAG_SFR=1 \
            -DMODULE_GNRC_SIXLOWPAN_FRAG_MINFWD=1 -DCONFIG_GNRC_SIXLOWPAN_FRAG_RBUF_SIZE=1 \
            -DMODULE_GNRC_SIXLOWPAN_IPHC=1

H_INC = -I$(ROOT) -I$(ROOT)/sys/include/  \
            -I$(ROOT)/core/lib/include/  \
            -I$(ROOT)/core/include/  \
            -I$(ROOT)/cpu/native/include/  \
            -I$(ROOT)/drivers/include/  \
            -I$(ROOT)/boards/native/include/  \
            -I$(ROOT)/sys/net/gnrc/pktbuf/include/  \
            -I$(ROOT)/sys/net/gnrc/pktbuf_static/include/  \

# Include our special build file
MAKE_INCLUDE_PATH ?= ..
include $(MAKE_INCLUDE_PATH)/Makefile.include

## Rules
1. You MUST NOT replace the original implementation of the target function with a stub.
2. Only modify the H_INC and H_DEF variables. Do not modify or introduce any other variable.
3. You are only allowed to modify the included header files in the harness file, where this is necessary to compile the harness with the target file.
4. You are also allowed to install missing dependencies using the run_bash_command tool. You have sudo access and can run "sudo apt-get install <package>" to install missing packages.
5. You are not allowed to create or modify any file directly using the run_bash_command tool.
6. If it is not possible to compile the harness with the target file, return a detailed analysis of why and empty updated_makefile and updated_harness fields.
7. Do not request full file contents using run_bash_command. Request only snippets, line ranges, or grep output.
8. Be proactive: identify as many include paths and definitions as possible before your first `makefile_validator` call to minimize iterations.

For example:\n * ```\n * if (IS_ACTIVE(FEATURE_FOO)) {\n *      do_something();\n * }\n * ```\n * @param[in]   macro   Macro to evaluate\n * @returns     1 if the macro is defined to 1\n * @returns     0 if the macro is not defined, of if it is defined to something\n *              else than 1.\n *\n * @note        This should only be used when macros are defined as 1, it will\n *              not work if the macro value is, for example, (1) or 1U.\n *\n * @note        Although this may seem to work similarly to the preprocessor\'s\n *              \'defined\', it is not entirely equal. If the given macro has\n *              been defined with no value, this will expand to 0. Also note\n *              that this is intended to be used with \'boolean\' macros that act\n *              as switches, and usually will be defined as 1 or not defined.\n */\n#define IS_ACTIVE(macro) __is_active(macro)\n\n/**\n * @def         IS_USED(module)\n * @brief       Checks whether a module is being used or not. Can be used in C\n *              conditionals.\n *\n * @param[in]   module   Module to check\n * @returns     1 if the module is being used\n * @returns     0 if the module is not being used\n */\n#define IS_USED(module) IS_ACTIVE(module)\n\n/**\n * @cond INTERNAL\n */\n/* Here a prefix "__PREFIX_WHEN_" is added to the macro. So if it was a 1 we\n * have "__PREFIX_WHEN_1", and if it was not defined we have "__PREFIX_WHEN_".\n */\n#define __is_active(val)              ___is_active(__PREFIX_WHEN_##val)\n\n/* With this placeholder we turn the original value into two arguments when the\n * original value was defined as 1 (note the comma).\n */\n#define __PREFIX_WHEN_1 0,\n\n/* Here we add two extra arguments, that way the next macro can accept varargs.\n *\n * If the original macro was defined as 1, this will have three arguments\n * (__take_second_arg(0, 1, 0, 0)), otherwise it will have two\n * (__take_second_arg(__PREFIX_WHEN_ 1, 0, 0)). The third zero is there just to\n * be compliant with C99, which states that when a function-like macro ends\n * with ellipsis (...) it should be called with at least one argument for the\n * variable list.\n */\n#define ___is_active(arg1_or_junk)    __take_second_arg(arg1_or_junk 1, 0, 0)\n\n/* Finally, we just always take the second argument, which will be either 1\n * (when three arguments are passed, i.e. macro was defined as 1) or 0 (when\n * only two arguments are passed).\n */\n#define __take_second_arg(__ignored, val, ...) val\n/**\n * @endcond\n */\n\n#ifdef __cplusplus\n}\n#endif\n\n/** @} */\n', 'stderr': ''}

The priority values</div><div id="25" class="line none">   25  * are "order" or "nice" values, i.e. a higher value means a lower</div><div id="26" class="line none">   26  * priority.</div><div id="27" class="line none">   27  *</div><div id="28" class="line none">   28  * ### Example:</div><div id="29" class="line none">   29  *</div><div id="30" class="line none">   30  * Given threads with priorities A=6, B=1, and C=3, B has the highest</div><div id="31" class="line none">   31  * priority.</div><div id="32" class="line none">   32  *</div><div id="33" class="line none">   33  * A higher priority means that the scheduler will run this thread</div><div id="34" class="line none">   34  * whenever it becomes runnable instead of a thread with a lower</div><div id="35" class="line none">   35  * priority.</div><div id="36" class="line none">   36  * In case of equal priorities, the threads are scheduled in a</div><div id="37" class="line none">   37  * semi-cooperative fashion. That means that unless an interrupt</div><div id="38" class="line none">   38  * happens, threads with the same priority will only switch due to</div><div id="39" class="line none">   39  * voluntary or implicit context switches.</div><div id="40" class="line none">   40  *</div><div id="41" class="line none">   41  * ## Interrupts:</div><div id="42" class="line none">   42  *</div><div id="43" class="line none">   43  * When an interrupt occurs, e.g. because a timer fired or a network</div><div id="44" class="line none">   44  * packet was received, the active context is saved and an interrupt</div><div id="45" class="line none">   45  * service routine (ISR) that handles the interrupt is executed in</div><div id="46" class="line none">   46  * another context.</div><div id="47" class="line none">   47  * When the ISR is finished, the `::sched_context_switch_request` flag</div><div id="48" class="line none">   48  * can be checked. In case it is set, the `sched_run()` function is</div><div id="49" class="line none">   49  * called to determine the next active thread. (In the special case</div><div id="50" class="line none">   50  * that the ISR knows that it can not enable a thread switch, this</div><div id="51" class="line none">   51  * check can of course be omitted.)</div><div id="52" class="line none">   52  * If the flag is not set, the original context is being restored and</div><div id="53" class="line none">   53  * the thread resumes immediately.</div><div id="54" class="line none">   54  *</div><div id="55" class="line none">   55  * ## Voluntary Context Switches:</div><div id="56" class="line none">   56  *</div><div id="57" class="line none">   57  * There are two function calls that can lead to a voluntary context</div><div id="58" class="line none">   58  * switch: `thread_yield()` and `thread_sleep()`.</div><div id="59" class="line none">   59  * While the latter disables (think blocks) the thread until it is</div><div id="60" class="line none">   60  * woken (think unblocked) again via `thread_wakeup()`, the former only</div><div id="61" class="line none">   61  * leads to a context switch in case there is another runnable thread</div><div id="62" class="line none">   62  * with at least the same priority.</div><div id="63" class="line none">   63  *</div><div id="64" class="line none">   64  * ## Implicit Context Switches:</div><div id="65" class="line none">   65  *</div><div id="66" class="line none">   66  * Some functions that unblock another thread, e.g. `msg_send()` or</div><div id="67" class="line none">   67  * `mutex_unlock()`, can cause a thread switch, if the target had a</div><div id="68" class="line none">   68  * higher priority.</div><div id="69" class="line none">   69  *</div><div id="70" class="line none">   70  *</div><div id="71" class="line none">   71  * @{</div><div id="72" class="line none">   72  *</div><div id="73" class="line none">   73  * @file</div><div id="74" class="line none">   74  * @brief       Scheduler API definition</div><div id="75" In this regard,\n * the thread of the MAC layer implementation has the highest priority and\n * threads on the application layer have the lowest priority. The communication\n * between threads is handled by the kernel\'s @ref core_msg functionality and\n * by the @ref net_gnrc_netapi. Most of the times IPC will take place between\n * threads of neighboring layers for packets that traverse the network stack up\n * or down.\n *\n * Due to the design of @ref net_gnrc "GNRC" and the nature of inter-process\n * communication, it is crucial for a new module that introduces a new thread\n * to follow a certain programming construct if it desires to interact with\n * other threads without blocking the system: Utilizing an `event loop`.\n *\n * Hence, a thread for @ref net_gnrc "GNRC" will usually consist of four basic\n * steps.\n *\n * 1. Initialize a message queue (note that its size **must** be a power of two,\n *    see @ref msg_init_queue())\n * 2. register for a @ref net_gnrc_nettype\n * 3. wait for a message\n * 4. react appropriately to a message and return to 3.\n *\n * ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~ {.c}\n * void *_event_loop(void *arg)\n * {\n *     static msg_t _msg_q[Q_SZ];\n *     (void)arg;\n *     msg_init_queue(_msg_q, Q_SZ);\n *     gnrc_netreg_entry me_reg = GNRC_NETREG_ENTRY_INIT_PID(\n *                                      GNRC_NETREG_DEMUX_CTX_ALL,\n *                                      thread_getpid());\n *     gnrc_netreg_register(GNRC_NETTYPE_IPV6, &me_reg);\n *     while (1) {\n *         msg_receive(&msg);\n *         switch (msg.type) {\n *             case TYPE1:\n *                 callback1();\n *                 break;\n *             ...\n *         }\n *     }\n *\n *     return NULL;\n * }\n * ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\n *\n * @note As an example have a look at the event loops of @ref net_gnrc_ipv6 and\n * @ref net_gnrc_rpl\n *\n * Receiving / Transmitting Packets\n * ================================\n *\n * Packets can be received or transmitted by interacting with the @ref\n * net_gnrc_netapi.\n *\n * Receiving Packets\n * -----------------\n *\n * The reception of a @ref net_gnrc_pkt from another thread is handled by the\n * @ref net_gnrc_netapi module. In order to receive a @ref net_gnrc_pkt of a\n * specific type, it is necessary to register for the appropriate @ref\n * net_gnrc_nettype first. Your thread will then be able to receive certain\n * commands defined in the @ref net_gnrc_netapi module (e.g. @ref\n * net_gnrc_netapi::GNRC_NETAPI_MSG_TYPE_RCV) for all @ref net_gnrc_pkt\n * "Packets" that your thread registered for.\n *\n * The following example will sketch how to receive incoming and outgoing UDP\n * traffic on port 80.\n *\n * ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~ {.c}\n * void *_event_loop(void *arg)\n * {\n *     static msg_t _msg_q[Q_SZ];\n *     msg_t msg, reply;\n *     reply.type = GNRC_NETAPI_MSG_TYPE_ACK;\n *     reply.content.value = -ENOTSUP;\n *     msg_init_queue(_msg_q, Q_SZ);\n', 'stderr': ''}
